# Text Elements
Lecture 3.1 Give automaton over {0, 1, 2} accepting all words containing substrings 12 or 21  ^1LFO4F3o

Lecture 3.2 Give an Automaton over {0, 1} that accepts all words not containing the substring 11  ^bmPnSuXy

Let be an arbitrary finite alphabet. Let be a nonempty string in *. Prove that the language L consisting of the single string

is regular.

Give a proof by construction describing a finite automaton that ends up in an accepting state only if it reads the string
. ^5teWA0BD

q2 ^X2451ey6

q1 ^30YQ2heJ

q3 ^JOHdOmSv

Write down explicitly such a construction (state diagram) of a product automaton when A is the set of all strings over {0,1,2} 
accepting the strings containing 12 as a sub-sequence and B is the  set of all strings over {0,1,2} 
accepting the strings containing 21 as a sub-sequence. ^K4gv174r

A = {0, 1, 2}, containing 12 ^xENc7dGQ

B = {0, 1, 2}, containing 21 ^35XRyr3x

 ^sn1Ipwyb

Closure Under Union ^CPypgFBB

complement of w1 ^TiF9jVpx

NFA ^WJyUYuGS

Star Operation ^5YZWYaaA

q1 ^YG8XbiEg

q ^U1KBNzAq

q2 ^lGUa8Fwq

If A is regular and B is a Subset of A then B is regular as well

- False
- 0*1* is regular, it can be accepted by a finite automata, however 0n1n is not regular
- A is the set of all words, B is just the palindromes
    - we know that B will not be accepted


Two things
- subsets of a regular language are not necessarily regular
- if a language is not regular, its compliment will not be regular as well ^M1Ee6GWp
